  (Now must we praise the Guardian of Heaven's kingdom,
  The Creator's might, and his mind's thought:
  Glorious Father of men! as of every wonder He,
  Lord eternal, formed the beginning,
  He first framed for the children of earth
  The heaven as a roof; holy Creator!
  Then mid-earth, the Guardian of mankind,
  The eternal Lord, afterwards produced:
  The earth for men Lord Almighty. -Thorpe ㅵ킶-)

  *The lyf short, the craft so long to lerne,
  th' assay os hord, so sharp and conquerynge,
  The dreadful joye, alwey that slit so yerue:
  At this mene I by Love, that my felynge
  Astonyeth with his wonderful werkynge
  So sore iwis, that what I on hym thynke,
  Nat wot I wel wher that I flete or synke)

  (When that April with his shoures soote
  The droghte of March hath perced to the roote,
  Of which vertu engendred is the flour;
  Whan Zephirus eeok with his sweete breath
  Impired hath in every holt and heeth
  The tendre coppes.....)

  *J.L. Lowes밻 General Characteristics of Chancer 78죇킕п Prologue톩 ?톓 래쒨덦
?봞. Persons of every sort and condition represented in the Prologue had been
intimately known to Chaucer Through years crowded with experience and observation.
What the portrait actually do, all conjecture aside is to strike the delicate
balance between the character, in the technical, Theophrastian sense of the word,
and the individual- a balance which preserve at once the typical qualities of the
one and the human idiosyncrasies of the other.

ballad, originally a dancing song, is a short-story told in song or verse, or a song that
tells a story, simple in plot and metrical structure divided into stanzas told
impersonally or with connotative and dramatic objectivity, ascribed to and circulated by
oral tradition among people culturally homeogeneous.

  * David Daiches: A Critical History of English Literature, 145죇.
In the Middle Age Greek science was only available in fragmentary and often distorted
from through Latin translations from the Arabic, for the Moslem world were earlier
heirs of Greek thought; now it became freely and directly available. No wonder
that Renaissance thinkers came to regard the Middle Ages simply as an
obstacle standing between them and the pure knowledge of the classical world.
The ages of "Gothic superstition", which was all the 17th and, 
still more, the early
and middle 18th century could see is the Middle Ages, were so regarded because
thy blocked the light of classical culture.]

 Wrastlyinge is a very good exercise....so that it be with one that is equal in strength
or somewhat under, and that the place be soft so that in fallinge they bodies be
not bruised.....Bowling, however, is to be utterly abjected of all noble men, in
likewise foot ball, where in is nothing but beastly furie and extreme violence.

땇밻 솪 퇫떋 ?멪*킕п 촿씉 п몹? 칊?랭톓 븸럼?밻뷒 metaphorical?돘 둧줭?
image늏 ?쫨?봞.
  * Divers doth use as I have heard and know,
  When that to change their ladies do begin,
  to moan and wait, and never for to lin(cease),
  Hoping thereby to pease (calm) their painful woe.
  And some there be, that, when it chanceth so
  That women change and hate where love hath been,
  They call them false, and think with words to win
  The hearts of them which otherwise doth go.
  But as for one, though that by chance indeed
  Change hath outworn the favor that I had,
  I will not wail, lament, nor yet be sad,
  Nor call her false that falsely did not feed;
  But let it pass, and think it is of kind(by nature)
  That often-change doth please a woman's mind.
  Petrarch랭?톩 램촻멤램 ?킕븸 래쒎 죇래 ?쫨?봞. 픮톋씉 땇톩 늏쩫텈 п몹? 틭킕밻

  * E.Legouis: A Short HIstory of English Literature, 78죇. Gorboduc abdicates in
favour of his
two Sons, Forrex and Porrex. These two princes soon full to dissension-as did
Eteocles and Polyneices-and the younger kills the elder. The queen, who more
dearly loved the elder, having killed his brother in revenge, the indignant people
rise in rebellion and murder both king and queen. Then follow civil war,
anarchy usurpation, and the death of usurper.

쟧?밻 ?멪뾦래봞.
  *One day I wrote her name, upon the strand,
  But came the waves and washed it away;
  Again I wrote it with a second hard,
  But came the tide and made my pains his prey
  Vain man, said she, that dost in vain assay
  A mortal thing so to immortalize,
  For I myself shall like to this decay,
  And ere my name be wiped out likewise
  Not so,(quoth I) let baser thing devise
  To die in dust, but you shall live by frame;
  My verse your virtue srare shall eternize,
  And in the heavens write your glorious name
  Where, whenas death shall all the world subdue,
  Our love shall live, and later life renew.
  땇쒊륾 래뾦
